# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Configuration File Parsing and Override Chain

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement configuration loading: the INI file parser, the environment variable override logic, the default values per section, and the sensitive config value masking for the /api/admin/settings endpoint.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

```json
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've successfully created the answer.json file with a comprehensive analysis of Grafana's configuration loading system. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

**Core Configuration Files:**
- `pkg/setting/setting.go` - Main configuration loading with INI parsing and masking logic
- `pkg/setting/provider.go` - Settings Provider interface implementation
- `pkg/setting/expanders.go` - Configuration variable expansion system
- `pkg/api/admin.go` - Admin settings endpoint implementation

**Configuration Loading Chain:**
1. **INI Parsing** - Uses `gopkg.in/ini.v1` library to parse configuration files
2. **Environment Variable Overrides** - `applyEnvVariableOverrides()` method checks for `GF_SECTION_KEY` format variables (generated by `EnvKey()` function)
3. **Configuration Expansion** - `expandConfig()` function expands `${VAR}` and `$__file()` syntax using plugin-based `Expander` interface
4. **Sensitive Value Masking** - `RedactedValue()` function masks passwords, secrets, tokens, and keys; `RedactedURL()` handles credential redaction in URLs
5. **Admin Endpoint** - `AdminGetSettings()` returns redacted settings with access control filtering through `getAuthorizedSettings()`

**Dynamic Features:**
- `DynamicSection` struct allows runtime environment variable overrides via `SectionWithEnvOverrides()` method
- Default values loaded from `conf/defaults.ini` are merged with custom configuration and environment overrides
- Settings returned through `Provider.Current()` are automatically redacted for sensitive values

The answer.json file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with all files, symbols, execution chains, and detailed narrative explanation.

URLs containing credentials are masked using the RedactedURL function (pkg/setting/setting.go:711) which redacts passwords and usernames from URLs while preserving the rest of the URL structure.\\n\\nThe admin settings endpoint is implemented in pkg/api/admin.go. The AdminGetSettings handler (line 29) calls hs.getAuthorizedSettings which filters the settings based on user permissions through access control evaluation. The settings returned by SettingsProvider.Current() (pkg/setting/provider.go:118) are already redacted through the OSSImpl implementation, which applies RedactedValue to each configuration value before returning it in the SettingsBag.\\n\\n**Configuration Loading Chain:**\\nThe complete configuration loading chain is: loadConfiguration -> load defaults.ini -> apply command-line overrides -> load custom configuration -> applyEnvVariableOverrides -> expandConfig -> SettingsProvider.Current() with RedactedValue masking -> AdminGetSettings endpoint with access control filtering.\"\n}\n",
